{=This is a common form in the Titus texts. Royal has this apparently\n
diphthongal spelling of the first element also at the same place in\n
the running text, but not in the place where it appears again in\n
Titus. It also appears in Royal once in the Life of St Margaret. It\n
looks to be a form common to whatever lies behind T and R or, since\n
it appears in all but one of T\'s texts, maybe it\'s a NW Midland\n
spelling and R has got it via the NW Midland version behind T. The\n
same kind of spellings happen also in the words "anywhere", "anywhither"\n
and "nowhither". Compare Orm\'s OwwHAR and NAU+ spellings in Trinity\n
Homilies and Vices and Virtues in the East Midlands, and NOU+\n
spellings in Laud Misc 108 hand A and the Nero version of Ancrene Riwle\n
in the SW Midlands. d\'Ardenne & Dobson (1981) print NOWHER=}\n
